                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-athletics"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Jake Smolinski</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/athletics">Oakland Athletics</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 29</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">5' 11" / 205</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">OF</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>2/9/1989 (29 y, 1 m, 1 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=5408&position=OF#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2007 June Amateur Draft - Round: 2, Pick: 6, Overall: 70, Team: Washington Nationals</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=5408&position=OF#contract" >$0.8M / 1 Years (2018)</a>
                        </div>
                    </td>

                    
                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=9898">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Smolinski avoided arbitration by agreeing to a one-year, $775,000 deal with the Athletics on Monday, Jane Lee of MLB.com reports. (11/27/2017)</div></td></tr>

                <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><table class="player-page-news"><tr>

                    <td>2/19/2015</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/texas-two-step-rangers-of-led-by-choo-martin/">Texas Two-Step: Rangers OF Led by Choo & Martin</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=11752">Paul Sporer</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>

            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        
        
        
        
        
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Rangers lack a clear left fielder entering 2015, and that makes Jake Smolinski an interesting sleeper in deep formats. Smolinski was exceptional in his rookie 2014 season, hitting .349/.391/.512 in 92 plate appearances. Those numbers were carried by his unsustainable .458 batting average on balls in play, and his minor league numbers suggest his power potential is limited. Still, he stole a few bases, walked frequently, and rarely struck out in the minors. Smolinski was not considered to be much of a prospect, and he could face competition for playing time from Michael Choice, Ryan Rua, and even Mitch Moreland in left field. However, unless the team signs someone else, Smolinski should get a real shot in 2015. His best-case scenario is likely .260 with 15 home runs and seven steals, but that makes him draftable in deep formats. (Scott Spratt)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Smolinski’s red-hot 92 plate appearances as a rookie in 2014 could earn him a shot at the left field job for the Rangers this season. His moderate power, speed, and walk rate make him a viable sleeper in deep formats.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Aside from two brief major-league stints in 2014, Smolinski spent more than eight years toiling in the minor leagues in the Washington, Miami, and Texas systems. He finally earned an extended look in the majors last year, playing 76 games between the Rangers and Athletics. The 27-year-old outfielder doesn't have the range to play in center, or the arm for right. Not many teams are going to clear a spot in left field for a platoon guy who contributes a .193/.281/.367 slash. (Scott Strandberg)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Smolinski is not fantasy relevant in any format.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Smolinski is known for one big skill: his ability to mash left-handed pitching. The right-handed slugger owns an impressive .290/.361/.505 line in 238 plate appearances against southpaws in his career, and even if he was not quite that sparkling in 2016, he still managed a .796 OPS against them. Smolinski also racked up a career high in playing time last year, but that added time in the lineup also meant more time facing righties, which dragged his overall line down to .238/.299/.345. Smolinski is headed into his age-28 season, and he could be in line for his share of playing time in a flexible Athletics lineup considering he can fit into all three outfield positions. That said, his lack of a consistent starting role, weak side of a platoon, and lack of substantial power or any speed means his fantasy value is limited to deep formats at best, if not only daily leagues against weak-to-medium southpaws. (Dylan Higgins)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>With the ability to mash lefties and play all three outfield positions, Smolinski has what it takes to fill a solid fourth outfielder role for Oakland, especially considering his age. As far as fantasy squads are concerned, however, this limits him to deep formats for now -- although he certainly gets a bit of a bump in leagues that allow daily roster moves.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>
